## \#10 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2018-07-07T15:35:31.598Z Reads: 1388

```
The typical setup will be our dual direct drive setup with our 110mm wheels which will use a Kegel Adapter but we'll offer an ABEC Adapter for those that want to use ABEC wheels. We'll probably offer an adapter for our Pneumatic Tires we're also trying to release. I am a bit hesitant as obviously with the larger wheels we reach a higher top speed.

@BruSkater - No launch date yet.. still testing. Just decided to show what it's looking like. :slight_smile:

@Mikenopolis - I think the current design we have would be a better option. I try to make sure everything in the past compatible but it's pretty hard.. To design a better system, you sorta need to start from scratch. Sucks...
```

---

## \#18 Posted by: skatardude10 Posted at: 2018-07-07T15:51:34.504Z Reads: 1171

```
12S / 65kv direct drive / 110mm wheels = 30 - 36mph.

I think it'd be great if the ideal speed we're designed around 10S, so those who want to go faster can run 12S... Push 40mph if they want. I'd want to go faster and personally would love to see 80-85kv DD.
```

---
## \#19 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2018-07-07T15:55:29.303Z Reads: 1184

```
@FredrikHems would be nice.. but the motors are pretty big already. Motor can itself is 70mm diameter and that's because we're using a thicker motor can for increased durability.

@BruSkater a bit over 30mph and we specifically use 12S. I don't see any point in 10S as for $40-60 dollars (difference from 10S4P vs 12S4P) you get a huge benefit for the higher voltage and increased watt hours.

@skatardude10 I'm very hesitant on offering higher speed setups.. We might in the future but as of now our main focus is the everyday rider.
```

---

## \#68 Posted by: bandrews510 Posted at: 2018-07-09T14:33:52.588Z Reads: 746

```
Delta to WYE transformations in Electrical Engineering is often the division or multiplication of sqrt(3) depending on which one you are going from.
![delta-star-1|690x456](upload://yQbd9StAAFvTtJyjDqjZak1eTD9.jpg)
```

## \#87 Posted by: mmaner Posted at: 2018-07-11T00:03:07.048Z Reads: 597

```
Aluminum pulleys will wear out faster than steel pulleys, about 1/3 the lifetime depending in how you ride. I think your problem maybe the 20t pulley, I got a lot more skips when I was running 20t, less mesh because the diameter is larger.
```

## \#92 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2018-07-11T13:29:04.192Z Reads: 600

```
Larger diameter will increase the number of teeth in mesh with the belt.  You might be trying to say that more teeth in mesh is worse for skippage, but the number of teeth in mesh will certainly be more.
```

## \#95 Posted by: JetskiMark Posted at: 2018-07-14T07:00:14.455Z Reads: 631

```
@torqueboards These motors look interesting.

I am interested in a 4WD set up with pneumatic tires. Torque is more important to me than speed.

Precision trucks sound good too. Any chance of having an adjustable base plate option? Something similar to the Don't Trip Euphoria Truck's adjustable base.

https://www.dtskate.com/ProductDetails.asp?ProductCode=1x%2DEuphoria%2DAdjustable

As most of you already know, you can make your board more stable at speed by running a split angle setup. This means your front baseplate is at a higher angle than the rear. When you do this, the turning is done more from the front than the rear, sort of like a car. The popular and stable Landyachtz Evo deck, increases the front baseplate angle by 9 degrees and reduces the rear by the same amount. It would be fantastic to easily adjust your baseplate angles to what works best for you.

On my traditional and electric boards, I wedge most of my front trucks and dewedge some of my rear trucks. It is not all about preventing speed wobbles. It's good for long distance pumping and it also gives your board a "surfy" feel. It would be great to not have to bother with wedges and the bent hardware they cause.

I am looking forward to these motors being readily available for a fair price.

Best of luck.
```

[quote="pat.speed, post:60, topic:61152, full:true"]
@torqueboards would it be possible to have the motor winded in wye for 50kv? ## \#102 Posted by: JohnTakesPhotos Posted at: 2018-07-17T06:33:03.922Z Reads: 549

```
@everyonewhowantstousepneumatics

An axial direct drive with pneumatics isn't going to work, the only exception being one with stupidly large brushless motors wound to a very low kV. The beauty of a reduction system is that the amplification of torque is directly proportional to the gear ratio. 
Decreasing the kV of a 6374 motor doesn't amplify the torque as a reduction does.
```

---

## \#106 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2018-07-17T09:20:02.847Z Reads: 546

```
[quote="pat.speed, post:101, topic:61152, full:true"]
It would work with normal firmware, just run canbus between the rear Vesc and canbus between the front vescs then connect both lots through split ppm
[/quote]

No - because the firmware would not send most power to the front wheels at low speed and rear wheels at high speed -- and wouldn't send braking to the rear wheels except hard braking to the front wheels, on a linear split.

This could be added, though - like a traction control module in the software.

With my firmware mod it is possible to adjust different acceleration and brake power at front and back axle.

## \#109 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2018-07-17T15:32:55.704Z Reads: 557

```
[quote="JohnTakesPhotos, post:102, topic:61152, full:true"]
@everyonewhowantstousepneumatics

An axial direct drive with pneumatics isn‚Äôt going to work, the only exception being one with stupidly large brushless motors wound to a very low kV. The beauty of a reduction system is that the amplification of torque is directly proportional to the gear ratio.
Decreasing the kV of a 6374 motor doesn‚Äôt amplify the torque as a reduction does.
[/quote]

but decreasing kv does increase torque and its directly proportional to current, you could say that's it's beauty.   there are many vehicles with hub motors successfully running much bigger wheels such as with a bicycle and with a low kv.   you could call a bicycle hub motor stupidly large if you want and it's true you could get more power out of a smaller mid-drive with pulleys, but if the hub motor is larger no pulley is necessary and just as good efficiency can be gotten if not possibly better as well as many other benefits.
but i hear you and at some point the wheel becomes too big for the motor and its kv and it will be less efficient.
```

---
## \#110 Posted by: JohnTakesPhotos Posted at: 2018-07-17T23:56:51.966Z Reads: 550

```
[quote="Hummie, post:109, topic:61152"]
but decreasing kv does increase torque and its directly proportional to current
[/quote]

Torque is determined by the number winds and the strength of the magnets in the system. To lower the Kv you have to increase the number of winds and for any given volume of copper you can fit around a stator, increasing the turns of the wire decreases the current throughput because the wire has to be thinner. 
That's why hubs heat up more (and are always going to be less efficient than a satellite system), you can't rewind a 3000w 6374 for torque and expect to be able to push 3000w through it again.


[quote="Hummie, post:109, topic:61152"]
there are many vehicles with hub motors successfully running much bigger wheels such as with a bicycle and with a low kv.
[/quote]

An e-bike uses a stator engineered for torque - it has a shit tonne more magnetic poles and motor teeth than recased 12t14p 6374. 

[quote="Hummie, post:109, topic:61152"]
but if the hub motor is larger no pulley is necessary
[/quote]

You can't just make the motor larger and call the system more efficient! 

[quote="Hummie, post:109, topic:61152"]
but I hear you and at some point, the wheel becomes too big for the motor and its kV and it will be less efficient.
[/quote]

:+1:
```

---
## \#111 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2018-07-18T00:17:30.481Z Reads: 565

```
[quote="JohnTakesPhotos, post:110, topic:61152"]
> but decreasing kv does increase torque and its directly proportional to current

Torque is determined by the number winds and the strength of the magnets in the system. To lower the Kv you have to increase the number of winds and for any given volume of copper you can fit around a stator, increasing the turns of the wire decreases the current throughput because the wire has to be thinner.
That‚Äôs why hubs heat up more (and are always going to be less efficient than a satellite system), you can‚Äôt rewind a 3000w 6374 for torque and expect to be able to push 3000w through it again.




no you cant rewind a rated 3000w motor for low kv and expect the same power output and eff but you can make a bigger motor that has therefore less electrical resistance and will have the same electrical efficiency and also greater mechanical efficiency than the original 3000w motor with a pulley

![|20x20](https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/user_avatar/www.electric-skateboard.builders/hummie/40/31081_1.png) Hummie:

> there are many vehicles with hub motors successfully running much bigger wheels such as with a bicycle and with a low kv.

An e-bike uses a stator engineered for torque - it has a shit tonne more magnetic poles and motor teeth than recasede 12t14p 6374.

if you look into it i think you'll find the torque potential is limited by the diameter of the interface and the volume of the materials and their properties.  with many magnets and teeth youre splitting those magnets and teeth up.  you end up with double the amount of magnets and teeth but each of them with half the strength.  i looked all over to find this out and have was told this straight from the horse's mouth...of the guy who wrote this very well regarded book https://www.amazon.com/Design-Brushless-Permanent-Magnet-Machines-Hendershot/dp/0984068708
i was insistent that it wasnt the case for a long time based on "torque motors", which have much greater accuracy and smoothness but seemingly not greater torque per volume of materials with the same airgap and all


![|20x20](https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/user_avatar/www.electric-skateboard.builders/hummie/40/31081_1.png) Hummie:

> but if the hub motor is larger no pulley is necessary

You can‚Äôt just make the motor larger and call the system more efficient!

if you make the motor larger, and it's primary loss was copper, especially if it's a slow turning hub motor with very low iron losses, yes making the motor bigger makes it more efficient as, just as you said above, the wire can now be thicker.

![|20x20](https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/user_avatar/www.electric-skateboard.builders/hummie/40/31081_1.png) Hummie:

> but I hear you and at some point, the wheel becomes too big for the motor and its kV and it will be less efficient.

:+1:
[/quote]

had to add inside

but...yes adding more poles adds more torque.  so yes more magnets and poles you can say adds more torque as it lowers the kv,  but youre trading copper losses for iron. which may be good and ideal in some cases depending how fast the motor goes largely.  that's my take on it all.  happy to hear any disagreement!
but besides that point i also still think a direct drive is capable of the same efficiency as a pulley drive in our typical application.  maybe not ideal on the steep uphill but overall.   going up the steepest hill...i think you could use a bigger motor with the right kv and you'd be as efficient.
```

---
## \#112 Posted by: JohnTakesPhotos Posted at: 2018-07-18T00:55:09.285Z Reads: 518

```
[quote="Hummie, post:111, topic:61152"]
if you look into it i think you‚Äôll find the torque potential is limited by the diameter of the interface and the volume of the materials and their properties. with many magnets and teeth youre splitting those magnets and teeth up. you end up with double the amount of magnets and teeth but each of them with half the strength. i looked all over to find this out and have was told this straight from the horse‚Äôs mouth‚Ä¶of the guy who wrote this very well regarded book https://www.amazon.com/Design-Brushless-Permanent-Magnet-Machines-Hendershot/dp/0984068708
i was insistent that it wasnt the case for a long time based on ‚Äútorque motors‚Äù, which have much greater accuracy and smoothness but seemingly not greater torque per volume of materials with the same airgap and all
[/quote]

Yeah, I know. Also generally by increasing the teeth, you increase copper fill. 

I was thinking more along the lines of the physical restraints imposed on a system when you make the motor larger, which was why I said you couldn't call 'the system more efficient" as opposed to "the motor more efficient".  You're right - a larger motor is more efficient than a smaller one given they both operate in the same conditions. The bone I'm picking at is the design of the system - efficiency isn't just for the motor, it's the collective efficiency of all the subsystems together.
```

---
## \#113 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2018-07-18T01:06:13.214Z Reads: 529

```
id have thought increasing the teeth would likely decrease the copper fill.  not that ive compared.  i imagine with double the teeth if you keep the same overall iron content, so instead of a 2mm thick tooth its now 1mm, the copper content could potentially be the same here with 1mm slots instead of 2mm and each of those slots now having half the fill,  so equal....except when getting more and more teeth there is a mechanical limit and they have to be so thick to stand up to vibrations and physical forces, especially so on a skateboard, so at some point the smaller teeth necessitates having less copper eventually as it needs to be iron with the bigger teeth so they dont bend or break.  (although thinking about it again, alone here,  if the stator were designed to have teeth with  no slots, with the diameter being complete iron, that would give a lot of support and maybe you could get away with the 1 turn per tooth motor im talking about below..and benefits of no cogging and smooth coasting)

but surely with more teeth you COULD get better copper fill if you just decreased the ratio of iron to copper.  and maybe that would work well and making me want to try modeling motors again

but in adding more teeth and dropping the kv that way, as apposed to doing it with more turns of wire, ..id like to see how that would go.   It would be probably more work to build but assuming the teeth are still strong enough, at lets guess 36 teeth, and before with 12 teeth the motor needed maybe 10 wire turns to get to the desired kv, maybe now it would need a third of that, and at maybe 3 turns..and going along those lines maybe if  50 teeth are strong enough you could do a single turn in the slot and then you could maybe have a cast piece inserted instead of trying to fit in cylindrical wire, or have the slot just the right shape for a shape wire, and therefore get 100% fill as apposed to even best case with cylindrical wire is roughly 85%.and still achieve the same kv.  but the iron losses at speed would suck and now it's an uphill monster only.  and surely not so simple and its assuming the motor were designed so that all those small magnet fields went where they were supposed to go


back on point...how many teeth does the stator have @torqueboards
```

## \#146 Posted by: Luvafreeride Posted at: 2018-08-02T15:50:58.386Z Reads: 429

```
I'm wondering if some skaters might like a smaller 5" or 125mm
 pneumatic to go with the new direct drives? Maybe even an airless?
```

---
## \#147 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2018-08-02T16:08:52.563Z Reads: 471

```
@Luvafreeride - Was harder to go 125mm since there's not much space for any air. I also don't think we need all the options.

We'll have a 110mm 75A wheels which should be more then you need for a urethane option.

I originally tried going 140/150mm pneumatics but overall 160mm was a better option. That way your rim can actually be a bit bigger and you can have a 7" or even 8" pneumatic tire as well. Otherwise 5.5" to 8" is a fairly big jump. Everything needs to be scaled down with a smaller tire as you'll need space for air. Evolve even tried 5.5" tires before but scraped the idea. I think 6.5" would be the smallest. Either way you would typically need a specific deck to fit any wheels over 97mm.

I even looked at making 125mm urethane on our rims but I don't think there's much benefit. The 110x65 will have thicker urethane 40mm thick and 65mm wide vs with our rims a urethane 125x50 would be 20mm thick, 50mm wide. If you asked me, I'd take the 110x65 if you're going urethane.
```

---

## \#183 Posted by: Epskampie Posted at: 2018-08-15T15:17:28.149Z Reads: 439

```
If it's really anywhere near $700 then I'm definitely out. The way I see it, it's 2 really big motors + custom truck + development costs.

2 big motors: (let's go for [the most expensive ones)](collections/electric-skateboard-motors/products/electric-skateboard-motor-6380-170kv): 2 *  $135 = $270
Really nice precision truck: around $130
Development costs: $???

Total: $ 400 + ???

So around $400 to $500 seems like a fair maximum to me. Of course, I know this math doesn't exactly add up, but if it's much more I'll just pray that the Carvon torquedrive comes back in stock, or that the Chinese clone this idea soon. :wink:
```

## \#188 Posted by: deucesdown Posted at: 2018-08-15T16:11:53.865Z Reads: 423

```
$135/motor is for large manufacturing runs with slim profit margins. These motors are heavily customized, with additional machining and parts for the wheel interface.

Really nice precision trucks are more like $1000. The cheapest precision trucks are around your price.

@torqueboards went all out and got Riptide for all the rubber parts.

Also warranty/support and spare parts. And cost of doing business in the great US and A.

Dexter deserves to make some profit for his efforts as well. I imagine his level of investment is getting pretty high, and he seems to be filling all the gaps with new developing products!
```

## \#191 Posted by: deucesdown Posted at: 2018-08-15T16:43:36.060Z Reads: 410

```
[quote="Epskampie, post:190, topic:61152"]
price himself out of the market
[/quote]

There are many segments to the market. The low end is covered, and for most of us, leaves us wanting.

The mid end does not exist because the necessary improvements to the low end cannot be done for incremental increase in costs/price.

The high end market does exist, because this is what it costs at the moment, to achieve what we want.
```

## \#192 Posted by: Epskampie Posted at: 2018-08-15T17:14:39.015Z Reads: 400

```

---
## \#193 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2018-08-15T17:23:40.740Z Reads: 420

```
@Epskampie yeah, unfortunately.. to do things right it ends up costing more.

We've worked on this design quite a bit and have tested tons of different variations and options to build a powerful and reliable direct drive setup. R&D costs money and takes time.

There's just no point in using casted trucks, crappy bushings,, crappy bearings.. just to save a bit. It ends up becoming a regretful purchase. There's also no passion for us in offering lower quality products and unhappy customers. We'd prefer to release products that are different then what's already available which are more reliable and higher performance.

These motors are designed and will be priced for customers that want the quality and performance. If there is no market for it then we simply won't sell it.

Either way, I think even you will be happy about the pricing once it's officially said. :) We simply just don't want to make any promises just yet.
```

---
## \#194 Posted by: Epskampie Posted at: 2018-08-15T17:39:53.335Z Reads: 414

We simply just don‚Äôt want to make any promises just yet.

## \#196 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2018-08-15T17:48:47.784Z Reads: 441

```
[quote="deucesdown, post:191, topic:61152"]
The low end is covered, and for most of us, leaves us wanting.

The mid end does not exist because the necessary improvements to the low end cannot be done for incremental increase in costs/price.

The high end market does exist, because this is what it costs at the moment, to achieve what we want.
[/quote]

This is so true.  There are "toys" and "tools" and, for the most part, if you want a tool, you need to make it yourself or get only a **tiny** number of premium brands of prebuilt ... none of which use hub motors or come from California or Australia... and all of which are $2k+

I read so many people saying "I want to do DIY to save money" and it's always the biggest facepalm.  Buy cheap china hub motor shit if you want to save money.  That's like saying I want to build a Lamborghini by hand because the Ford is too expensive to buy

I firmly hope these new direct drive are in the "quality tool" category, aren't listed for-sale until they're in-stock, stand-up to snow and brine, and price is the last thing to be decided, in order for the rest of that to be true.
```

## \#292 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2018-10-16T23:38:53.139Z Reads: 404

```
[quote="sayekim, post:291, topic:61152, full:true"]
With 97mm?
[/quote]

Well 62kv would work very well with 110mm and 107mm for 10S and 12S (25.9mph - 31.9mph) (41.6km/h - 51.4km/h)

With 97mm it'd be a bit torquey and with pneumatics it'd be a bit too fast, but I personally think that's the best compromise.  I'd mainly want to use direct drive on short decks with tails that are otherwise hard to electrify...
```

## \#351 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2018-11-11T23:31:51.415Z Reads: 386

```
@PXSS - Only ABEC/Kegel.. maybe test an option to use our pneumatics but haven't tested yet. I don't think there are any other great options otherwise. Motor can is 70mm diameter. You can go 90 or lower but you'll end up damaging your motor can but it would/should still be perfectly fine. They just won't be pretty no more. :smile: 

@pixelsilva - Yeah, we'll do a rounded inside lip but we tested it with the chamfer and there were no chunking.

@sn4pz - supposedly, yes.
```

[quote="torqueboards, post:320, topic:61152, full:true"]

The 83A wheels seem to ride better than the softer ones.  Don't let the number fool you, test them out.  The 'thane is so deep that 83A feels downright cushy.

## \#479 Posted by: Lunasi Posted at: 2018-11-25T04:29:46.680Z Reads: 374

```
It's based on 12s on the 75kv model with 110mm wheels, 34 miles per hour was literally where I topped out and I was mostly on flats. Bottom end torque is good, not quite as good as belt but if anything I loved the acceleration curve, was very comfy. Once she gets moving she takes off fast. Motors don't get that hot, trucks have heat dissipation built in.
```

## \#484 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2018-11-25T04:36:17.431Z Reads: 368

```
[quote="deucesdown, post:476, topic:61152"]
* Is the 35mph based on 12s with 110mm wheels? **Yes, with 110s on 12S.**
* Will we be able to purchase the wheel adapters separately? **Yes, can purchase adapters separately.**
* how‚Äôs the torque compared to dual 6355 or dual 6374? **I don't notice the difference much. Mostly, it's a totally different feel since you don't feel belts at all. I'm also a slow rider.. Need more testers :smile:**
* how are the brakes, especially at high speed? **Brakes are strong or more tame. You'll just have to set the settings within the VESC. During testing brakes were too strong.**
* do motors get hot? **They haven't got hot yet. There's just so much surface area for cooling. It's one of the reasons why I didn't design a hub motor.**
* what‚Äôs the 45mph option, and what voltage/wheelsize is it based on? **12S, 110MM**
[/quote]

My comments in bold.
```

---

## \#532 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2018-11-25T15:40:04.383Z Reads: 347

```
Hummie is able to use a much longer stator due to it being in-wheel. I tried to fit longer but it was nearly impossible while keeping it reliable. It would also push our setup to use a much longer hanger. Our stator is 52.8x40 but I believe we can fit a stator up to about 45mm with sensors.
```

It‚Äôs probably the logistics and the setup. Unlike Caliber and Paris , they don‚Äôt have the capital to spout out Trucks, much less separate trucks from a set and have it latter repaired with one later in case it needs to. Then you have to think about whether it‚Äôs msnagnle by the inventory system , and then you have to think about whether or not the cost of adding all that extra work is worth it. 

[quote="rusins, post:533, topic:61152"]
but weight is more important for my little brother
[/quote]

You threw weight out the window the moment you choose the big hangers and dual motors in them. Unless you make it a small battery, no matter what build you make , it‚Äôs going to be a heavy MF
```

## \#544 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2018-11-25T21:09:59.692Z Reads: 361

```
[quote="Friskies, post:537, topic:61152"]
What kind of temps are the magnets rated to?
[/quote]

We are using N42SH magnets. We haven't had any issues with heating. Trying to get more out there in the wild so we can do more testing but there's a ton of cooling so I doubt it would be a problem. We had 2-3 different hub motor versions which we've tested in the past. I'd like to think I've checked everything off as far as having any heating issues but always room for improvement.

[quote="hexakopter, post:539, topic:61152"]
Have you tested the motors with 80mm/90mm wheels?
[/quote]

90mm's would do great.. 80mm would be cutting it short. Probably wouldn't use 80mm.

[quote="jbruce, post:542, topic:61152, full:true"]
@torqueboards would this truck be way too big for a jet spud and look really weird?
[/quote]

Should be fine. I'm sure, you've seen short boards with a 218mm Truck.

With wheels on our DD setup is only about 10-15mm wider than our 218mm setup. It's barely noticeable.

[quote="evoheyax, post:543, topic:61152"]
I‚Äôm excited to race these with hummies hub.
[/quote]

Should be interesting. :smile:
```

## \#661 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2018-12-14T17:49:42.636Z Reads: 327

```
@jadatmag

Lower KV will give you more torque. 75KV
Higher KV will give you a higher top speed 90KV

You can also use a smaller wheel size for more torque.

We've also increased the stator size (for the upcoming pre-order) as well which would make them one of the biggest direct drive motors.
```

## \#699 Posted by: rusins Posted at: 2019-01-31T11:07:57.421Z Reads: 337

```
[quote="niv, post:695, topic:61152"]
Can I get away using 85mm Kegel‚Äôs?
[/quote]

The motor diameter is 70mm, so 85mm wheels will fit, but you won't have much clearance between the ground and the motors. Then again, that's always the case with small wheels, so decide for yourself. With my Caguama belt setup, I have around 12.5mm clearance between the ground and the belts, which seems to be fine. The motors and motor mounds will get scratched by pebbles either way.

In your case though, a 15mm difference in diameter will mean 7.5mm clearance between the motor and ground. I believe that's small enough where your motor will be constantly pushing small pebbles and debris out of the way. Unless you live somewhere with superb quality roads, I would go for bigger wheels / a different drive train. (Still waiting for swissboards.ch to come online :fist: ) 

P.S.
I get 24.2 mph (39kmh) in the calculator with your specs. Perhaps you forgot to change gear ratio to 1:1 ?
```

---

## \#702 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-02-01T00:29:49.827Z Reads: 315

```
@niv 
1. Yes, should be great for fast carving/tuning. We are also using all riptide bushings.
2. 85mm would fit but I wouldn't use it. The motors would be way too low to the ground. 90, 97, 100, 107, 110 would all be better options.
3. 12S on 75KV is about 35mph. 10S would be a bit under that.
4. Yes, I'd use 10S/12S ideally.

## \#711 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2019-02-01T02:36:31.672Z Reads: 307

```
Depends on your definition of efficiency. Per volt, a belt drive motor will produce more torque than a direct drive. Not that I like belt drive. Just that by putting a higher kv motor under gear reduction, you can achieve more torque per volt. I would assume based on that, a belt drive would get better efficiency.
```

## \#715 Posted by: Lunasi Posted at: 2019-02-01T04:54:01.209Z Reads: 317

```
I was doing about 20 miles on my 12s4p with a belt setup before, I'm getting roughly the same on the direct drive, if not a bit more. I find that you use a bit less energy than a belt drive, the 1:1 gear ratio means you get a really true roll like on a regular longboard. If you let go of your remote you don't feel yourself lose speed like on a belt drive, the extra tension in the belt drive actually costs more energy. I'd reckon I can get a few extra miles on the directs versus my belts, but I'd say they pretty closely compete.

FYI: I'm a fast rider so a slower rider would probably get more range than me

Oh and for the 35mph Dexter mentioned, keep in mind that's based on the current beta motors which are wound as 6355's when the final product will be wound for 6374. You might be able to get a bit more speed on the final product IMO than the current beta drives. I'm running on torqueboards vescs, torqueboards 12s4p 30q, sensorless, BLDC.
```

---

## \#756 Posted by: Lunasi Posted at: 2019-02-24T07:53:36.018Z Reads: 343

```
Typically a larger stator means a higher wattage which is why my top speed on dual 6355 belts is much lower than the same 190kv on a dual 6374.

If you've seen my race with Robin from lazy rollers at about 10 minutes in: https://youtu.be/b_uqtqzmRPQ

you'll note that our builds are nearly identical, he's on 12s5p with dual focboxes on 55's while I'm on 12s4p dual TB 4.12's on 6374's, both 190kv motors. He gets smoked by me at the end and can't catch up. All the love Robin! ‚ù§
```

## \#763 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2019-02-24T20:11:52.451Z Reads: 327

```
People say in use ideally you want the motor to run at about 85% of the no load speed with a load.  If ur running under that with a load maybe want to decrease the load somehow for better efficiency or get a bigger motor.  if you‚Äôre doing higher than 80% with a load you‚Äôre doing well with the motor size to load ratio.
```

---
## \#764 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-02-24T21:23:10.148Z Reads: 336

```
[quote="pat.speed, post:760, topic:61152, full:true"]
Lower resistance wires would provide more speed too? Less voltage drop across them so more to the motor?
[/quote]
precisely!

[quote="pat.speed, post:762, topic:61152, full:true"]
Yeah, winding resistances are already very low.
[/quote]
You also have to consider the **battery internal resistance** to calculate the net voltage "available" to the motors . A heavier person/higher wind resistance/going up a slope, all require higher current at a given speed and hence you have noticeably less net voltage to the motor hence less top speed. Also because of the current as the heat builds up, the winding resistance increases significantly, thereby also affecting the top speed. 

You can test it out by carrying a 20Kg backpack  / going up a hill / putting a cardboard on you chest to increase wind resistance.
```

---
## \#765 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2019-02-24T21:26:10.475Z Reads: 324

```
Also depends on things like whether you have efficient polyurethane longboard wheels or squishy pneumatic wheels.
```

---
## \#766 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-02-24T21:28:27.581Z Reads: 333

```
yep! 

So to say that **only** "KV and gearing" ratio dictates the top speed is totally wrong. <-not meant for you @b264 :D
```

## \#983 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-04-07T02:51:34.143Z Reads: 270

```
@gmurad @FranciscoV - PM me. Sorry guys. Really thought we had enough. :(

@jbruce DD Motor Seating - That's just a tolerance difference it's perfectly fine and designed that way. Should be fairly loose the other ones that are tight should a bit loose. Just as long as you're motor stator doesn't rotate.

Axles - We use standard bearings. You might need to fit them on. Originally, we got these shafts at 8.03mm (they f'ed up) and had to sand them down to 7.98mm, etc so that way we can get the orders out rather than waiting longer. They should fit great but if you need too. You can sand it down a bit. If any issues, let us know.
```

## \#989 Posted by: MasterSpoon Posted at: 2019-04-07T04:00:48.262Z Reads: 265

```
@jbruce do you have verniers / micrometers or any way to measure the shaft properly ?

Generally with machining due to deflection it's not uncommon to have a minor taper and if hand sanding it's hard to get it spot on. You need to know which part of the shaft is oversize so where to sand.

If possible remove the drive off the hanger or just get a loose 608 bearing and see if you can slide it onto the shaft. You want to remove all other variables, it sounds like the ABEC adapters are a bit tight so hopefully your not sanding the axle down if the fitment issue is with the adapter

If not you could do a redneck solution if the bearing goes on partway and get a sharpie and color in the shaft, try put the bearing on, where it interferes it will likely rub off the sharpie and that is where you need to sand. Rinse and repeat until your all done.
```

---
## \#990 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-04-07T04:01:40.396Z Reads: 253

```
You can also try different bearings. Some bearings differ very slightly. One might be easier to get on than another.
```

---
## \#991 Posted by: jbruce Posted at: 2019-04-07T04:05:18.064Z Reads: 249

```
its only a problem with the bearing shaft, not the wheel adapter @MasterSpoon sadly i also dont have any of those tools and the bearing currently wont slide on at all past the threads. @torqueboards ive tried 3 different bearings so far and none of them will go on past the threads

## \#992 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-04-07T04:07:01.437Z Reads: 255

```
You can put the axle on a drill with sand paper.. and drill. :smile: If not, I can try and send you another shaft if you're having too much trouble.
```

---
## \#993 Posted by: MasterSpoon Posted at: 2019-04-07T04:09:56.752Z Reads: 261

```
[quote="jbruce, post:991, topic:61152"]
ive tried 3 different bearings so far and none of them will go on past the threads
[/quote]

608 bearings are that common and have been around for that long that I would be honestly surprised if any where not 8mm +/- 0.001, they are ground finish so generally really good tolerance

If it won't go past the thread you may have a bur at the end, if you have an engineers file carefully add a chamfer at the transition. If you only have sandpaper get a piece of wood, put the sandpaper over the edge and use that to add the chamfer. You want to avoid just sanding the whole axle if it's just a bur at the transition
```

---
## \#994 Posted by: jbruce Posted at: 2019-04-07T04:12:34.850Z Reads: 257

## \#999 Posted by: MasterSpoon Posted at: 2019-04-07T04:27:35.237Z Reads: 258

```
@torqueboards what is the thread length on these ?

Thinking pretty much all cordless drills will have a big enough chuck diameter wise to take these axles, if the thread section was short enough could just pop one end in the cordless drill and get the axle not the thread and use the drill to carefully spin the hanger while you hold some sand paper on the axle on the other side. Still a bit barbaric but better than sitting there trying to manually sand the axles

A lathe would make it a 2 minute job, but guessing since jbruce doesn't have any measuring tools guessing doesn't have a lathe either :stuck_out_tongue: Edit, lathe would only be to hold and spin the hanger, if taking 0.03mm off then would still stick to sandpaper
```

---
## \#1000 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-04-07T04:30:53.592Z Reads: 251

```
Yeah cordless drill will work. Just take the axle off the hanger and fit it into the chuck. Apply pressure on the shaft part not the thread.. then drill and then test fit into the bearings. Shouldn't take too long. That's how we did it.
```

## \#1026 Posted by: jbruce Posted at: 2019-04-09T06:09:58.887Z Reads: 265

I‚Äôm not sure what type it was, just had it lying around. Remove both motors from the axle then take the axle part of the truck off of the base plate and stick one of the axle ends into a drill and tighten the drill Hold sandpaper on the other axle while spinning it. Takes some time so be patient.

## \#1027 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-04-09T08:34:14.272Z Reads: 272

```
@Jansen send us an email so we can take a look at it.

@AlanZhou Yours should of been sent out recently.

@kaaaaahle Don't take off the side hex screws as those are meant to keep the front motor cap on. Just the 6 TORX bolts you would need to remove. They are a tight fit so you'll need a rubber mallet to knock the pulley out and maybe a small screwdriver to lift it up. You also shouldn't have to deal with the axle issue. jbruce issue should of been a one-off issue.

@mikenyc Motors sit on the truck hanger and everything is press-fitted with the locknut.
```

## \#1032 Posted by: finges Posted at: 2019-04-09T15:32:54.476Z Reads: 249

```
I inititally mocked out drop through mounting on the Hummie... It looked like you had a little under .5 inches between the deck and the top of the motor. You would definitely have to sand out a motor well to make it work... I didn't feel comfortable with the amount of material that would have the be sanded and the structural integrity that would be compromised.

If you look at the first picture... you can see that with a top mount... it's about 1.25 inches from motor to the bottom of the deck. The deck itself is about .75 inches... if you routed out a spot to flush mount... you might get back .125 inches... Feel like it's not enough room
```

---
## \#1033 Posted by: Pedrodemio Posted at: 2019-04-09T15:48:36.912Z Reads: 252

```
You probably be fine, try first without routing the board and making the wells if necessary

I have routed mine to make the trucks leveled and had no problems so far

@finges same as I said above, if you routed so the truck being flat you will probably be ok even with deep wells, bet way to do this is to attach a sandpaper to the motor and run it slowly

The Hummie deck is really thick compared to normal decks and still have two carbon fiber layers inside
```

## \#1059 Posted by: rey8801 Posted at: 2019-04-10T18:16:02.943Z Reads: 250

```

```

---
## \#1060 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2019-04-10T18:25:42.293Z Reads: 259

```
Kv is the inverse of kt which tells torque per amp.  A motor of any size and a lower kv will put out more torque per amp, so u could have an elephant sized motor with 90kv and a baseball size motor at 80kv and the smaller motor will put out more torque per amp.   It will have greater electrical resistance so be more inefficient and possibly get so hot as to ruin the motor but for a short period it will put out more 

Unless u put a lot of current in the big and small motor (both w 90kv and let‚Äôs say 100 amps) the smaller motor will magnetically saturate the iron of the stator and it won‚Äôt be able to convert all those amps to torque as it should so while kv and kt tell how much torque u get per amp, there‚Äôs THAT limitation and ALSO km, which reveals torque to heat produced generally in the windings

So peak torque decided by kt (kv) and how much iron available, and continuous decided by the km of the motor and what heat it‚Äôs capable of getting to before it destroys magnets or windings or bearings
```

---
## \#1061 Posted by: rey8801 Posted at: 2019-04-10T18:37:49.618Z Reads: 250

```
There is some way so calculate the amount of current need to saturate the copper? I know thst depends on different factors but maybe there is a general law.
```

---
## \#1062 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2019-04-10T18:42:34.581Z Reads: 256

```
The copper windings increase their magnetic field strength without any limitations other than the resistance of the wire and burning up.  The electrical steel of the stator can support about 1.6 Tesla magnetic field strength before the relationship goes south and instead heat is increasingly produced.  So a motor w no steel wouldn‚Äôt suffer from magnetic saturation but then it will also take a huge amount of current and much electrical resistance with many coils to get close to the field strength helped with the steel
```

---
## \#1063 Posted by: rey8801 Posted at: 2019-04-10T18:44:36.646Z Reads: 249

```
Thst was always what I was wondering abou it. I see all the commercial Mott with steel stator but aluminium motor can. Do you think they go for the aluminum choice only for price and weight difference?
```

---
## \#1064 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2019-04-10T18:46:20.978Z Reads: 251

```
Most of them have a steel flux ring behind the magnets in the rotor.  If they don‚Äôt theyre wasting their magnets and not containing their field.  Steel behind the magnet will greatly increase its pull force.  For motors at the peak of performance they might use a carbon rotor and a hallbach array with the magnets.  Less weight
```

---
## \#1065 Posted by: rey8801 Posted at: 2019-04-10T18:48:06.520Z Reads: 252

```
I see. Then only like 1mm thickness is enough you don't need a thicker one to contain the field.

Most of the outrunner motor are open front and back. True thst the magnetic filed is eccentric but I would aspect some loss.
```

---
## \#1066 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2019-04-10T18:55:17.927Z Reads: 260

```
The shape of the field varies from what part of magnet it‚Äôs coming from with the field really coming out of the magnet‚Äôs sides but a 1mm thick mild steel ring doesn‚Äôt hold it.  There‚Äôs simulations on that main magnet page. Forget the name. But I found it way off and a lot more gets out. It‚Äôs a huge loss and if for example the motor used a 3mm thick flux ring it will greatly increase the pull of the magnets and then u could compensate for that on the stator side with less coils and therefore less electrical resistance.   It‚Äôs like getting a 250kv motor, with few coils and lower electrical resistance, and pressing on a 2mm steel sleeve and dropping it to 190kv.  

All these thin steel back irons we see with out runners are maybe good for a plane saving weight but for a motor on a board the thicker the better.  Especially a DD rolling along the road for protection
```

---
## \#1067 Posted by: rey8801 Posted at: 2019-04-10T18:56:55.784Z Reads: 259

```
Makes sense. Well I don't think most of the motors are more than 1mm steel. At least not the one I have. Good that I used 3mm mild steel. A pain to make it but seems worth it. Thanks for the explanation. Always super nice talk with you.
```

## \#1077 Posted by: Ashintar Posted at: 2019-04-12T22:22:59.684Z Reads: 280

```
Got a test ride in figured I share. 12s4p 90kv 90mm popocas 200 lb rider with gear got me 19 mi on spirited riding with headwinds it felt like everywhere to getting into battery cut off. https://strava.app.link/WjA1jJQYPV.  Torque feels really good on them but I only have a 10s setup to compare. I can say I'll be testing the durability of the cans xD ![IMG_20190412_161001|666x500](upload://2rzRanStbO1dd7DNkx09qDQpMGh.jpeg) . The only real issue I have is one the motors was loose I could pull it off and that one sounds like there a metal ring something loose but I couldn't find anything. The motor spins fine it just sounds different on spin up compared the other. Might just be that new setup overattentive to noises.
```

## \#1139 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-04-16T18:49:11.601Z Reads: 274

```
@McErono @epss4 @Ubbiedude The axles were originally 8.03-8.05mm. We had to sand them down to about 7.98-8mm. If you are using different bearings or purchased an ABEC set and we didn't install the wheels this issue might be more apparent.

You may have to sand the axle shaft. Put it on a drill collet and turn on the drill using 80 grit sandpaper or a bit more.

It was either that or everyone wait until the new axles are made. I'm sure, nobody wanted to wait any longer and some people have to wait longer. So we made the decision to send it out.

I will have new axles if anyone wants new axles but obviously there's a wait time.
```

---

## \#1142 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-04-16T19:00:03.264Z Reads: 273

```
@Ubbiedude They are standard. Clockwise to tighten. Counterclock to untighten. righty tighty lefty loosey. Email us.

If you're having trouble removing the axle there's threadlock so you may need to put some elbow into it and/or heat it up a slight bit.
```

## \#1150 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-04-16T22:03:10.128Z Reads: 286

```
@rusins me and finges planed to mount it drop through but the motors are bigger than expected. 

[quote="finges, post:1032, topic:61152, full:true"]
I inititally mocked out drop through mounting on the Hummie‚Ä¶ It looked like you had a little under .5 inches between the deck and the top of the motor. You would definitely have to sand out a motor well to make it work‚Ä¶ I didn‚Äôt feel comfortable with the amount of material that would have the be sanded and the structural integrity that would be compromised.

If you look at the first picture‚Ä¶ you can see that with a top mount‚Ä¶ it‚Äôs about 1.25 inches from motor to the bottom of the deck. The deck itself is about .75 inches‚Ä¶ if you routed out a spot to flush mount‚Ä¶ you might get back .125 inches‚Ä¶ Feel like it‚Äôs not enough room
[/quote]

![20190408_212558%20(2)|690x335](upload://gVyQoz9jgnMP672knjwKYtOc8fW.jpeg)

@FredXanadu its a wildboar-d crash pack bumper. Cut to size and epoxied where needed.

![20190417_000955|666x500](upload://qgIKeqNElFHimvIwcrdA5w02snJ.jpeg) 
![20190417_001021|666x500](upload://gxrnEPcdcKFQhynv36SfCGzGhSS.jpeg)

@torqueboards 
 [quote="torqueboards, post:1139, topic:61152"]
I will have new axles if anyone wants new axles but obviously there‚Äôs a wait time.
[/quote]

Thats ok! Just to let you know your own abec7 bearings from your 97mm wheels wont fit either. Tried bones red, oust9 and torqueboards abec7.

## \#1165 Posted by: LEE Posted at: 2019-04-17T11:24:17.599Z Reads: 269

```
Torque DD is 5.5 mm Barrett, R-Spec motor 3.5 mm Barrett.  This also has to be converted.
![image|666x500](upload://1jaDLXlc7ZyT3e8V2DaVr2wVUa9.jpeg) ![image|667x500](upload://u108zalOkmrNMEc5f3OyPiEPGB6.jpeg) 

As @esk8jpn says, the sensor connector also needs conversion.
The FOCBOX unity is a 2 mm pitch JST ph connector, and the Torque DD is a 1.5 mm pitch JST zh connector.
![image|375x500](upload://aakyDqCl3xm25Xs4hgxXbA3PRj.jpeg) 

The torque board sells conversion connectors.

https:///products/vesc-sensor-wires?variant=712409808919
```

---
## \#1166 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-04-17T11:25:55.800Z Reads: 256

```
No. It was a lazy build :innocent:

Hummie deck and mounted enclosure from bigben.
12s4p charge only bms, fuse, 4A torqueboards charger plug by pjotr.
DirectDrive and Bigwheels from Torqueboards.
Unity Enertion

So all I did is some modification on the enclosure (holes for switch and charging plug and a cutout to fit the truck baseplate), griptape, coating the matte hummiedeck with 2k, printing the x-things, soldering motor adapters, job done.

Its kind of my dreamboard and its not even more expensive than the raptor 2.1 on sale... which I am still waiting for a replacement since january.
```

---
## \#1167 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-04-17T11:28:40.895Z Reads: 247

If you are in the EU I can recommend these adapters: https://shop.elektro-skateboard.de/eigenbau-tuning/zubehoer/727/hall-sensor-adapterkabel-fuer-vesc

Not the cheapest but fast delivery
```

## \#1179 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-04-17T17:04:52.022Z Reads: 254

```
@McErono - TB DD will climb up steep hills but the downside to it is because of the lack of gearing ratio it will create more heat when ran hard. Ideally, you don't want to keep climbing up really steep hills back to back as it will create more heat. Eventually, you can/may burn a motor out will probably take a while but it is possible. To safeguard, just make sure you don't get the motors "too hot" and you're golden.

@rideTastic - You just need 2x 3.5mm to 5.5mm wire adapters for the motor wires. 2x Sensor Wires to plug into the unity.

@Eskate444 - Batch 2 should be about 30 days ETA.
```

---
## \#1180 Posted by: Pedrodemio Posted at: 2019-04-17T17:30:51.718Z Reads: 254

[quote="torqueboards, post:1179, topic:61152"]
TB DD will climb up steep hills but the downside to it is because of the lack of gearing ratio it will create more heat when ran hard. Ideally, you don‚Äôt want to keep climbing up really steep hills back to back as it will create more heat. Eventually, you can/may burn a motor out will probably take a while but it is possible. To safeguard, just make sure you don‚Äôt get the motors ‚Äútoo hot‚Äù and you‚Äôre golden.
[/quote]

That‚Äôs the perfect scenario I was trying to describe for the advantages for the temp sensor, you won‚Äôt be able to cook your motor, only loose acceleration 

If configured correctly you won‚Äôt loose brakes ever
```

## \#1193 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2019-04-17T19:07:27.107Z Reads: 259

Going slower and/or kicking a tad from a standstill will increase your range far more than using a tuck, but that does help too.

If you treat the motors as a ski-lift instead of a musclecar, your range will increase very significantly.

## \#1233 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-04-19T20:14:37.259Z Reads: 266

```
They are big. They may have a 6374 stator but are way bigger than a normal 6374 motor. Lots of metal, heavy duty stuff. They stay hot for a very long time after a ride (nothing bad in my opinion).

The R2.1 motors are very inefficient. Even compared to the old R2.0 motors you loose 20-25% range I guess.

Did a 7km run yesterday with two very steep but short inclines on my TB DD and my 12s4p reported 20% battery usage. (75kv 220lbs)![20190419_224533|374x500](upload://8CKT9rlxanbBJU6FrqYvF7NKgcm.jpeg)
```

---
## \#1234 Posted by: rideTastic Posted at: 2019-04-19T20:53:55.585Z Reads: 264

```
Is the torque of the DD 75kv the same as the raptor 2.1 ?
```

---
## \#1235 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-04-19T21:23:21.088Z Reads: 268

```
I can't compare them side by side... waiting since january for a replacement raptor 2.1. And my TB DD is 12s so wouldn't be fair to compare them. All I can say is the 75kv TB DD has more than enough torque for me... most of the time I am cruising in slow mode (62% throttle) on steep inclines I use full power and it flys!

Another short run (can't get enough of this board and sneak out whenever I can...) 6km, 16% usage. So I estimate 35-40km range on full charge. Battery is brandnew and had only one full cycle yet.
```

## \#1237 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-04-21T01:19:24.791Z Reads: 276

```
I think I found the cause of the slightly noisy motor. I tried to tighten the tolerances with teflontape. it did lessen the clearance between the axle and the motor but had no effect on the sound of the motor.

I believe its the C-clip. The brownish ring in the picture. It was quite shifted to one side not in the center of the big bearing. Centered it as good as possible and the motor sounds much better now almost identical to the other one :+1:![20190421_025827|375x500](upload://akxqm1UTOcabIrG1CoT28axaYIt.jpeg)
```

---
## \#1241 Posted by: skatardude10 Posted at: 2019-04-21T19:25:48.975Z Reads: 265

```
I rode the beta set (grain of salt here) with Jeffery's second iteration low speed brake fix on Acks fw. Braking wasn't as strong as my belts at low speeds, kinda came to a slow coast at best. I did have current control, and if toggling reverse I could reverse into full stop just fine if I remember correctly. When toggling reverse though, the rotational play on one motor would lead to rattling at that point though, and I didn't have enough time with them to properly shim the rattles away fully.

In general, less aggressive slow speed breaking but smooth as hell. I'd love to hear other people's thoughts who have done the low speed break fix on their vescs with this first batch of motors.
```

## \#1244 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-04-21T21:13:17.582Z Reads: 255

```
I don't consider braking on the DD's an issue. 100kg/220lbs and I have strong enough brakes... I guess thats quite subjective. batt regen for highspeed brakes, max brake current for low speed brakes.

But I noticed I had stronger brakes unsensored which is strange and new to me. As soon as my sensors started working (bad hall sensor adaptercables) the brakes got a bit weaker.

Glad I did go with the 75kv with my weight.

I would also be really interested if some of the other users like @Toughook and @LEE would chime in. I mean its quite clear by now I love the TB DD's A LOT! did I already mention how awesome the really big wheels are? :wink:
```

## \#1298 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-04-23T23:26:26.673Z Reads: 263

```
There is no problem with braking. I had to dial them down, they are strong! What people are talking about is that at 1-3kmh the brakes do not lock the wheels which is a non issue for most. You are not getting to a stand still on a decline.

Belt drives with FOC do lock up at that speed and I hate it. There is a whole thread about it somewhere. So I clearly prefer the behaviour of the DD.
```

## \#1304 Posted by: Winfly Posted at: 2019-04-24T07:34:40.445Z Reads: 287

```
![IMG_20190423_232957|690x323](upload://cYFtRKK6LffWCttHXidH0NBCYo4.jpeg) 

Finally got some data today. I was wearing a half shell, no pads on a unfamiliar board and remote I didn't trust myself to push faster. I would say I'm pretty impress by just the dual 90kv. I'm sure it would only get better when I complete the 4WD board. The wheels feels nice and soft but a little too big for my taste. Breaking is still the same, it's strong at speed but no low rpm break. It would put me to 5mph then I would have no break. This might be fine for some of you but definitely not ideal for San Francisco.

Setup is:
* Evolve Carbon Gen2
* Dual TB 90kv
* TB110
* 12s4p Sanyo 18650RX
* Unity
  * Motor 90/-60, batt 90/-30

**Data is recorded assuming 28pole pairs.**

First:
* distance - 2 miles of flats
* Speed - 20mph avg, 27mph top (only 68% duty)
* Efficiency - about 25Wh/mile avg (seems fair, I get around the same with Hummies)

https://metr.at/r/b1oaC
 

Second: 
* Distance - 0.5 miles steep uphill (California St, sections of 11,12,15% grade)
  * ![IMG_20190423_233728|234x500](upload://6ITcpqGOiXlLbGx4lP7H0Mxk45w.jpeg) 
* Speed - avg 14mph, 24mph top
* Efficiency - 75Wh/mile avg
* Temp - ~80F >>>120F (not so bad considering the speed I was riding up this hill)

![IMG_20190423_233931|234x500](upload://3jhNTNn2JecNawSiERgh7drm2Lp.jpeg)![IMG_20190423_234402|690x323](upload://oM1N0xNUKtTKiXevcigvvyU67Fm.jpeg) 

https://metr.at/r/DpKtk

Sadly @sofu's feather receiver broke down so we don't have telemetry to compare. @StefanMe pls fix.

She was quite sad. QQ
![IMG_20190423_232813|234x500](upload://qfHLpbKjHvnUWbS5YMPyoKbwcNj.jpeg)

P.S. forgot to mention and this is actually pretty important. Right after I got on top of the hill. One of the motor suddenly had a lot more resistance than the other. I felt it because the free coasting was a lot worse and then I hand spun it and found out. Not sure if it was a over heat issue because it could still spun with the throttle. But after a while it went back to normal. Maybe a bearing ~~ceased~~ seized?
```

## \#1364 Posted by: Pura-Vida Posted at: 2019-04-26T01:43:29.505Z Reads: 253

```
Hi AlanZhou,

I am novice with e-sk8, but I am an engineer for 26 years working for car, plane, military industries.
I can tell you that when something is supposed to rotate and get different constraint you are going to get heat, vibrations, so your efficiency and resilience will be worst....
Do a test: dry-run for 15 minutes at 30-50% of charge. Every 30 seconds you collect the temperature of both DD.
if running the test twice the same DD is heating more than it's twin brother, you are in a bad situation.
It is important to run the test at low to mid speed, as the data you want to collect are unwanted heat in relation with frictions.
```

---
## \#1365 Posted by: AlanZhou Posted at: 2019-04-26T01:44:41.777Z Reads: 253

## \#1388 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-04-27T00:03:08.877Z Reads: 260

```
every 2 hours for DH :slight_smile:

personally, for the TB 110s I bought that are on the TB DD @Winfly is using, I like Tektons:

https://seismicskate.com/product/wheel_bearings_tekton_ceramic/

super-precise and tolerances keep dirt out.

daily drivers are low precision, so to keep dirt out, I prefer grease as it keeps dirt out better than oil.

https://stokedrideshop.com/products/dragon-bearings-for-longboards-and-skateboards

The 'Endure' type uses the same grease as Hamboards, etc.  The only drag is they don't come with spacers.

Hope this helps.  TB DD FTW. :)
```

Yeah, that is kinda ridiculous. It makes sense to use light lubricant when you are pushing. When it's a vehicle, I don't understand why people are so anal about reducing bearing drag. In the grand scheme of things it's not a significant factor in efficiency.

## \#1391 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-04-27T01:55:51.964Z Reads: 259

```
Not to get off-topic, so insert:

> ![tumblr_nkahsm5Qnh1tkat9co1_400|352x318](upload://a7OvzVws9otUvnaPzZ7NmbxRtRt.gif) 

TorqueBoards is awesome... Dexter is awesome...  buy his many wares... hehe

... I've found that you can "reset" just about any longboard or motor bearing with Reel Butter Bearing Lube.

https://www.amazon.com/Ardent-Reel-Butter-Bearing-Lube/dp/B001H54MCO

Reel Butter isn't magic, it's not going to dissolve a tiny rock or anything, yet if you do clean them and flush them with this stuff.. well, even with the most expensive, crazy high-end ceramics I've ever had, always, very noticeable improvement with Reel Butter over the lighter oils.

Bones Speed Cream is still 4.5/5 tho :) good hunting!
```

## \#1449 Posted by: Winfly Posted at: 2019-04-28T19:04:03.085Z Reads: 243

```
QQ.. what's the overall max temp magnets and epoxy rated for? hummie's can to up to 250F. If it's over 200F I don't think we would have any problem beside not being able to read temp data.

I guess it also depends on how heavy you are.
```

---
## \#1450 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-04-28T19:12:12.968Z Reads: 246

```
Should be able to do 200F. I've burned out a few small motors in the past. You can feel it before it happens.

While you're riding the motor will struggle and typically the time it burns out is when you're climbing or scaling a hill and you stop and dump more amps on it in the middle of a hill. If you push it past that level it's toast. If you stop get off the board and walk up the rest of the hill. You'll save your motor. Let it cool down and ride again.

So best thing if you're going up a hill is to keep the momentum. Don't lose the momentum. Losing the momentum will put more stress/heat on the motors (any motors).

Typically, I think it's hard to burn out a motor on flat ground mostly uphill/downhill will you get all the added heat.

TB DD has quite a quite bit of cooling so I don't have SF hills anymore but you guys do. Test it and let me know.

So I'd climb a decent hill 1-2 times, how hot do the motors get? then climb the same hill again 3-4, 5-6, 6-7, 7-8.. 8-9.. .etc... 

If they always stay warm. you should be good to go.. If you know past 8-9 hard climbs they are pretty hot.. After 8-9 hard climbs stick to flats for 10-15 mins to let them cool.

If they never get hot enough for your standard routes... then you gravy. :smile:
```

---
## \#1451 Posted by: Pura-Vida Posted at: 2019-04-28T19:13:13.805Z Reads: 236

```

---
## \#1452 Posted by: LEE Posted at: 2019-04-28T23:44:20.628Z Reads: 241

```
Enclosure is [eboosted EVO40DS](https://www.eboardsperu.com/product/landyachtz-evo-39%E2%80%B3-ds-v2-4wd-applications/).  Very robust and easy to use.
The gasket is neoprene.
The use of a thick gasket slightly increases the capacity within the enclosure and provides more freedom in cell alignment.
Enclosures for double stack can be stacked with Unity and thin charge only BMS.
Thicker gaskets make this easier.

I will not use the AT wheel with direct drive.
The AT wheel is used for drive with gear ratio.
Riser is back and forth self-made 3d printing.
As for the filament being used, the front riser uses PLA.  The tailguard uses TPU.
```

---
## \#1453 Posted by: youseekcota Posted at: 2019-04-29T02:18:18.788Z Reads: 252

```
Initial review time. I just finished the Maryhill event, and it was so amazing. Completely closed course, well organized and well supported with food provided and EMT support which was put to good use. I had two boards, my Xerxes 14000 watt 4wd (actually laid down 12000 watts!) an my torqeboards direct drive. Had zero issues with the Xerxes, FVescs got up to about 150 but no more, motors didn't seem too warm after really going for it up the 1.8 mile hillclimb. 

Now, to the Direct Drive. First braking and acceleration were absolutely a joy and so so so buttery smooth. Braking power was certainly sufficient with this 2wd setup power was very good considering I was running 12s4p through 4.12 Fvescs. When I was aggressive with my last hill climb, I found the limits of the system. I experienced several cutouts under hard uphill acceleration. The motors certainly did get very warm, but not so hot that I couldn't comfortably touch them. I suspect my vescs got a real workout though. I've experienced cutouts with these vescs on a completely different system so I'm inclined to think the vescs were at fault. In a couple weeks I'll be getting two FVESC 6.6's back from repair and then I'll know for sure. But almost certain the vescs were at fualt, or my vesc settings weren't ideal.

I'd really have to give the DD a high review, for their buttery smoothness, the fact that they build up a relatively light board (20lbs vs 30 for my other board). When you're coasting it feels a lot like a traditional longboard which is fantastic. However it means that you won't get the drag from the belts that helps limit downhill speed. For flat terrain, this board really shines, Certainly goes just about as fast as anyone might like to go uphill too.
```

## \#1465 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-04-29T09:15:44.022Z Reads: 235

```
I still haven't got my replacement raptor but it's an easy choice for me.

Motors that last so far, a cushy backtruck with lots of urethane, more range, same or more power (still vague because of the thermalthrottling back in january but thermalthrottling at -2¬∞C is strange anyway) and then there is the hummiedeck which I love and no batterysag.

100m steep incline. The raptor came to a stop about half way up. Lots of battery sag and one motor over 100¬∞C within seconds. The TB DD does the same incline with ease several times and is accelerating from bottom to top.

The dual 6374 belt driven board has more torque and never ever got into temp issues. But its loud, not as smooth and in Switzerland I need a stealthy board.
```

## \#1484 Posted by: Static Posted at: 2019-05-01T14:49:01.512Z Reads: 242

```
I just went through this about a month ago. I've had road rash plenty of times skating, but this was the worst. This was the first time I didn't let it scab. Instead keep the wounds clean and moist and they will heal faster. Daily fresh dressing and petroleum jelly. 

Get a motorcycle jacket with armor
```

---
## \#1485 Posted by: brenternet Posted at: 2019-05-01T15:42:45.030Z Reads: 246

```
Drying wounds and letting them scab is regurgitated advice from the 40s. It's clinically proven that you will heal faster with moist, covered wounds. Scarring is also significantly reduced. 

You can even heal up/reduce a decade old scar by moisturising and plastering it for a month. This is common modern medical knowledge that just doesn't seem to have found it's way into western homes for some strange reason.
```

---
## \#1486 Posted by: Saturn_Corp Posted at: 2019-05-01T16:05:04.729Z Reads: 241

## \#1497 Posted by: gibber Posted at: 2019-05-07T12:37:25.997Z Reads: 238

```
I have personally used 3m Tegaderm for my wounds and it works - but it's not cheap.

Look up 'Tegaderm Road Rash' on Google and make your own decision but different types of clinical film wrap has been around for at least 20 years.  This is just one of the best.

---
## \#1498 Posted by: Aeroquiv Posted at: 2019-05-07T14:59:59.250Z Reads: 239

```
I used to work as a Surgical Tech and I exclusively use Tegaderm regardless of injury. Faster recovery and less scarring but you do have to watch out and drain exudate. There are products that design around this and absorb excess drainage, but they can get pretty pricy.

Oh, also some body parts are not compatible with Tegaderm, specifically, hands and feet. They sweat too much and cause the adhesive to prematurely fail. It's possible to use Benzoin to increase adhesive strength, but it is also an irritant.
```

---
## \#1499 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-05-07T23:29:21.531Z Reads: 227

## \#1528 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-05-10T20:34:09.564Z Reads: 242

```
@youseekcota Current TB DD Batch #1 doesn't have the proper hall sensor pcb so it doesn't record temps so not too sure.

As long as the motor doesn't get hot you should be good. You'll only burn them out if they get way too hot so if they are warm. You're not close to burning them out. Typically, the easiest way to burn out the motors is climbing steep hills without momentum, back to back.

@skatardude10 I was going to do the Kegel Core but that will have to come around later. I decided to push through anyways with the current as changing now will delay the AT wheels way too long :sob:

@ThomasL If you do go with the AT wheels, make sure you go with 75KV. We haven't tested yet but it should be decent enough.

@AlanZhou - You should email us. Wrong channel for any updates like that here.
```

---

## \#1555 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2019-05-14T16:29:28.608Z Reads: 238

```
"Motorized" implies it had motors added later, and not at the time of manufacture.

Most of our esk8 were manufactured with the motors.

Hence, they are "electric" and not "motorized".
```

---
## \#1556 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-05-14T16:48:25.865Z Reads: 240

```
I know what you mean. Thats english vs. german, here motorized is something with a motor no matter if manufactured with it or added later. Cars, Scooters, ebikes all are motorisierte fahrzeuge.

https://www.dict.cc/?s=motorisiertes+Fahrzeug :wink:

Gopro is charged... but I am still working. I hope I can show you my motorisiertes fahrzeug tonight.

@Pura-Vida Here are the rules in Switzerland https://www.tcs.ch/fr/tests-conseils/conseils/types-de-vehicules/segway-et-vehicules-tendance.php

Both are standards. One is VESC standard the other is Hallsensor standard. I have no idea why nobody is switching to a straight VESC plug setup on the motors IF the motors are intended for esk8 use only.

## \#1668 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-06-07T11:45:17.163Z Reads: 211

```
They need to be soldered. 3 soldered 3.5 to 5mm adapters per motor.

But only one sensor adapter cable is needed per Motor.
```

@rideTastic I recommend the big evo 39‚Äú, the evo falcon I have is kind of short (after you know the hummiedeck everything feels short). with 97mm wheels and a singlestack enclosure you wont have a ton of clearance but certainly enough. I use a doublestack enclosure and have to use like 4cm of risers on 97mm wheels and still not enough clearance.

Seems no issues from first batch, both motors spin free and quiet, zealous bearings go on perfectly, fits genuine flywheels snug but not too tight, got a quick ride in before laying down (I have to redo my ppm mapping because full brake is neutral/50% on throttle, coast is 75% and full acceleration is 100% gah!) and these drives are powerful! I only got to ride with 33v battery so far, so it's charging up tonight for a good ride tomorrow. 

I've set them to 80/-80 motor each and 65/-12 battery each. I can't wait to put these through their paces tomorrow, Friday and the rest of this weekend. 

I've got the 90kv versions on 10S5P, 35¬∞ rear and 50¬∞ front and they are still super maneuverable and agile! I think I'm liking the stock bushings, but may change out the rear boardside for a firmer WFB chubby for some extra stability and to offset the extra leverage from the 35¬∞ baseplate. 

Glad I managed to fit it all in: ![20190626_212910|243x500](upload://vZv8FNLxf60WI6511cEx04c1mQn.jpeg) ![20190626_215409|243x500](upload://hEdh0gq2Lkhk3Ckk6JvsiNop2oC.jpeg)

## \#1837 Posted by: chsknight Posted at: 2019-06-28T18:20:10.860Z Reads: 177

```
Just wanted to leave this here for anyone else to use.  I wont get a chance to try this "fix" until this weekend, if I even choose too.

## KEGEL/ABEC ADAPTERS Bearing Seat Too Tight

The bearing seat on the kegel/abec adapter can be a bit too tight. If it is too tight it‚Äôs about .20mm - .40mm too tight. This can restrict the free spin of the motor.

To fix it, you can space out the gap between the direct drive motor and the wheel adapter.

1. The fix for this is to remove the wheel. It‚Äôs a tight fit and may require you to use a soft mallet to remove the wheel. You can hit the wheel from the inside of the wheel towards the outer side of the axle.
2. Undo the 6 bolts that hold the kegel/abec adapter together. We use a T20 Star/Torx Bit as this will prevent any stripping of threads.
3. Add 2 layers of masking tape on 3 sections of the Direct Drive Motor. We add them in-between the bolt holes on top of the cavity hole for the wheel adapter. This will sit the wheel adapters a bit higher once the wheel adapter is tightened.
4. Spin the direct drive motor and notice the amount of free spin.
5. Re-assemble the wheel adapter and secure the 6x M4 Star Bolts to secure the wheel adapter.
6. Spin the direct drive motor again after securing the wheel adapter and the free spin should be very similar. It is typically easier to free spin once you attach the wheel to the setup.
7. Once completed, you should be perfectly fine. Re-assemble the wheel onto the direct drive and secure your lock nut.
8. When securing the lock nut. The wheel will tighten on the adapter a bit more this is designed and meant to do this.
9. Confirm the lock nut is secure and is not applying too much force on the bearing but yet tight enough that there is no horizontal play on the axle.
```

---

## \#1850 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-07-02T19:40:12.622Z Reads: 188

Don't worry about some strange sounds while handspinning the drives. My first batch drives sound a little different all the time. The C clip position changes sound, temperatures etc.

Further you see the freespin of my 1st batch motors brandnew. Play with the tension of the wheelnut. Get them as loose as possible without the motors starting to be movable on the hanger.

## \#1854 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-07-03T03:39:51.469Z Reads: 184

```
Motors should all roll smooth. Typical issues if they aren't rolling smooth would be the following:

* Axle nut restricted/too tight.
* Circlip restricted/too tight.
* Wheel adapter restricted/too tight.
* Bearing restricted/too tight.

If they don't roll smooth, check the possible issues above. If any issues, send us an email. :smile:
```

---
## \#1855 Posted by: 0r3sk8 Posted at: 2019-07-03T06:26:26.133Z Reads: 195

```
I wish I hadn‚Äôt deleted the video I sent over to Dexter so you can verify you‚Äôre experiencing the same thing, but basically it sounded like a bearing that wasn‚Äôt spinning, or something was rubbing against one of the spinning parts or some such thing. The problem only started about 100 miles (one month) into riding the board. The motors were otherwise both spinning just fine, no problem there just the constant wahhhhhhhhhh, wahhhhhhhhh in one motor. 

I had taken the wheels off and replaced them. Checked the clip as instructed and did a general inspection. Nothing changed to that point. But to me it sounded distinctly like a bearing issue or plastic rubbing on metal or something generally rubbing at high speed. 

It was too familiar of a rubbing noise and so I asked Dexter if it was possible to try a little lube. He said sure. I dug out my bottle Riptide Speed Lube ‚Äúdry formula‚Äù. Tipped the motor to one side (inner facing up) and put a few drops (5-6 drops maybe; not much) in and around the entire rubber seal right below the clip that holds the motor together. I didn‚Äôt remove the cover or open anything, just let it soak in around the ‚Äúdust cover‚Äù. Worked the motor around a little by hand, let it rest for a few hours and applied another 6 drops or so and let it rest overnight. The squeal was diminished within minutes and once the oil penetrated it seems to be set for good. I attached a pic of the motor part Im talking about even though I‚Äôm sure you will know. I just want to be as clear as possible because these are expensive motors. I don‚Äôt want to be the cause for someone ruining their investment. 

Maybe @torqueboards can clarify that this is all kosher, but it seems to have worked and my motors appear no worse for wear.  Although I‚Äôm still a little suspicious, so much so that I ordered a 2nd set of DD‚Äôs to compare and to have in case this first set needs to be returned. Many here have mentioned how quiet the motors are and mine have never really been super quiet, at least not like those stupid skooters around town. Those things are dead quiet and maybe the DD‚Äôs aren‚Äôt meant to be, but I haven‚Äôt received the second set yet to compare. The pair I have now sound a little more like ‚Äúdrills‚Äù (that‚Äôs not exactly right, but kind of close). I like the sound in fact, but they aren‚Äôt dead quiet. 

What @McErono showed in the video above is quite normal. What I experienced was a high pitched squeal that was far, far worse than ‚Äúnot what I expected‚Äù and clearly sounded like something was wrong. As I said I had been riding the board for weeks before the squeal started.

That sound is no longer there since I added the lubricant. I can at least say that. 

I would see if Dexter says a-ok because I don‚Äôt want to give someone bad advice, but this is what has worked for me so far. 

I hope it gives you something to work with because I know how frustrating it is relying on ‚Äúcustomer service‚Äù. I think TB‚Äôs staff is probably overwhelmed with lots of stupid questions and our constant enquiries for ‚Äúwhere‚Äôs my shit‚Äù? making it hard to separate and respond to genuine issues. 

If I can be any further help don‚Äôt hesitate to ask. 

 ![image|375x500](upload://fFDZpYG0qqgpdavDvY9JaTr40cM.jpeg)
```

## \#1918 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2019-07-15T19:31:24.742Z Reads: 173

```
[quote="Richcan, post:1917, topic:61152"]
I always thought Direct Drive would run cooler not being a hub driven motor being inside of PU. They would have no problem with heat issues?
[/quote]

somehow the heat has to get out from the stator windings in the center of the motor where probably 95% of the heat is produced.  you can have the rotor uncovered such as with a direct drive instead of hub motor, but the heat still has to get from the stator either to the skate hanger aluminum or to the magnets and then out through the outside of the rotor.  there's ferrofluid which is a magnetic liquid which can fill the gap and allow conduction otherwise youre pretty much limited to convection heat transfer to the magnets and its rotor.   Its the same obstacle bike hub motors have and they use ferrofluid (magnetic fluid to fill the airgap) with heatsinks mounted on the outside of the motor

whats the actual phase resistance and kv as seen on the vesc tool?
```

---

## \#1932 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-07-16T17:11:19.300Z Reads: 174

```
@Jansen but I do understand this is your second set of DDs right? No one else has the same issues so far - my guts telling me it is not an issue with the DDs. That behaviour of running fine and then after a short pause not having any power is in my opinion not motor related.

Your sensors are not working (running in sensorless mode?) and the temp sensor gives crazy values? (Screen shows 130 and 180C in the unity app) there are sensor-adapter cables with different pin allocations. My adapter cables from torqueboards were working fine, some others I had to swap pins to make em work. But usually they work or they don't work at all.

You are talking about a "horrible sound" while cogging. I had the exact same thing going at first with my DDs. First thing was I calibrated my remote in slow mode instead of fastest mode = cutouts. Second thing (horrible sounding cogging) was a firmware issue on the unity when I was accelerating fast from a standstill. Firmware 23.43 sorted that out completely. 

I am going over 30mph at the moment, pushing it hard on steepest uphills - no issues whatsoever. BUT I still avoid 35mph were some guys like murloc experienced issues (complete lockup of the motors - not DDs).

@rideTastic the unity setup via app in combination with the DDs doesn't get any easier. Its foolproof. The only time I used the unity tool (tcp bridge and usb-c) was to reduce the remote ppm deadzone. 30sec and you are good to go. And I did every firmware update via Bluetooth so far, one of them even on the road in the middle of a ride.
```

---

## \#1938 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2019-07-16T17:51:41.583Z Reads: 171

```
It's a long thread and I'm not sure what all ur prob were but to test the motor I'd move wires around a lot, pull on them, then do repeated foc testing and look at ohms. If it's not the phase wire connection it could be a short within the windings.  That more so gives cogging and bad power and extra heat continuously vs something loose 

  maybe move phase wires a lot while running on bench while adding a lot of resistance with a gloved hand maybe.  And do sensorless to narrow it down
```

## \#1957 Posted by: ThomasL Posted at: 2019-07-19T12:07:39.885Z Reads: 164

```
Guys, any advice on how to increase low speed brakes on the 90KJV with the Unity. I like their smoothness but there is almost none around 3mph.

Any advices are welcome :)
```

---
## \#1958 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-07-19T14:15:20.107Z Reads: 163

```
@ThomasL - There are two options to increase brake strength.

1. Increase braking regen from -15 to -30 amps and that should give you more then enough brake. It was more then enough for me even going downhill but if you want even more 2nd option.
2. Use current mode and limit reverse speed and you can get stronger brakes as the motor will go in reverse instead of braking. You just have to be mindful of it. I haven't tried this one yet personally but I'd imagine it's similar to Boosted's setup which works nicely too.
```

---
## \#1959 Posted by: ThomasL Posted at: 2019-07-19T14:51:02.045Z Reads: 156

```
Humm, strange, my braking regen is already around -35.
So by switching from Accelerate/brake to Accelerate/reverse it should become stronger ?


Will try later and post it up.
```

---
## \#1960 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-07-19T15:11:58.333Z Reads: 161

```
Yeah, what I think I do automatically that I haven't noticed is if I'm at low speed.. I'll throttle it and then brake. Seems to help with braking IMO on belt drive or DD.

If that doesn't work you'll probably have to try the 2nd option.
```

---
