```
@Jansen they shouldn't be doing that unless they are overheating and/or unless your not giving it throttle throughout the hill. Are you using sensors? If so check what your motor heat cutoff is. If you have a metr.at try that to get more data.
```

## \#2014 Posted by: 0r3sk8 Posted at: 2019-07-23T22:35:03.544Z Reads: 170

```
Just take off the wheels and pull the motors. You don‚Äôt have to remove the motors though. I just turned my board on the side to expose the ‚Äúinner dust ring‚Äù and retainer clip and put a few drops around that ring and let it soak in. You‚Äôll see that it‚Äôs not an airtight seal and there‚Äôs enough of a seam to apply literally just 6 or so drops, soak  and maybe reapply. I only had the issue with one motor though. You too? 

I can‚Äôt say I would recommend WD40 because it tends to act more like a solvent and would destroy any grease in and around the bearings that was installed at the factory. Any decent lubricant should be fine, I prefer ‚Äúdry‚Äù lubricant because it makes less mess. They sell similar stuff at bike shops also, but I specifically used ‚Äúriptide speed lube‚Äù.  Pic repost for reference. 

![image|375x500](upload://fFDZpYG0qqgpdavDvY9JaTr40cM.jpeg) 



Let‚Äôs see what Dexter says but initially he said go ahead and give it a shot. I have t done enough riding yet to say this is a permanent fix or not. But I have put about 50 miles on it since I did this and seems to be fine. Certainly the sound went away immediately. Literally within 5 mins of the first application.
```

---
## \#2015 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-07-23T23:27:36.330Z Reads: 170

```
Could be a dried out bearings. Sounds almost like it. Not really sure otherwise why the motor would sound like that.

I typically re-oil my standard outrunner boards usually every 2-4 weeks when I use them frequently and everything just runs a lot more smoother. At least for me the dirt and grime would just cake on after time.

@rideTastic use bearing oil. Don't use WD40. I would think WD40 might dry it out more.

Try it and let us know. We'll have to double check all bearings and make sure they are lubed up.
```

## \#2023 Posted by: McErono Posted at: 2019-07-24T14:13:11.639Z Reads: 165

```
both not normal. all should be tight. 

these motors seem perfectly fit to the tb110 kegels in terms of adapter tightness and axle lenght. if you can move that motor this much sideways the thread on the axle is way too short for these lazyrolling wheels.

as soon as my motors have a little bit of play on the hanger (by loosening the axlenut too much) they make a horrible grinding sound (vibrations) but that goes away as soon as I tighten the nut again.

did you try to put some electrical tape on top of the motors/under the adapters? try adding 2-3 speedrings on the outside of the wheels to get a tight fit and compare the sound.

my first gen TBDD still have no issues at all other than some rare random noises and clicking that comes and goes with temp changes.

btw. the big bearing at the back is filled with grease, so oiling (get yourself some bones speedcream or something) is not that effective. just remove the bearing seal carefully with a razor blade and make sure its not dry.
```

---

## \#2060 Posted by: Richcan Posted at: 2019-07-26T03:28:59.116Z Reads: 164

```
@Hummie How can you check resistance? Positive an negative with ohm meter? Also some of these hard spots when spinning? Shouldn‚Äôt check those spots while slowly turning? Sounds like rubbing on magnets?
```

---
## \#2061 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2019-07-26T03:46:49.433Z Reads: 162

```
If the magnets are rubbing I can't imagine a solution but if mechanically the motor were fine u can check it electrically doing the bldc or foc test on the Vesc connected to a computer.  With the new vescs maybe it's not the same but id think ud still be able to get these numbers.  The phase resistance will be so low it's not gunna show accurately on a multimeter.  U could use an inductance meter if the rotor were off and either number can show how the winds are doing.  Easiest on vesc


People w tight motors it could be axial compression on either side and u could grind down the big c clip. Maybe.
```

## \#2069 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-07-26T15:30:01.957Z Reads: 155

```
@epss4 @richcan @Menjos @JeffDj **Drive Wheel Adapter Too Tight**

It could be the drive wheel on the top of the motor. You may need to space the gap a bit.

You can use tape and/or M4 washers to space the gap. Once the gap is spaced it should spin freely. 

I believe, the adapter is smashing the front bearing which adds resistance to the motor spinning so we want to space it out a bit.

@Jansen damn.. you just got all the luck. Are both motors having the issue or is it just one? It's most likely the heat issue that everyone's mentioned. I'd try what @McErono mentioned. 

@JeffDj you might need more lube on your bearings.

@Richcan Magnets are fine. I doubt magnets would be any issue. The magnets are surrounded by a thick steel retainer on both ends. They aren't going anywhere. :)

@McErono @Skatardude10 Appreciate you guys sharing your experiences.
```

---

## \#2090 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-07-26T18:42:23.187Z Reads: 167

```
Do not remove the bolts on the front motor cap which are on the side of the motor. Those don't need to be removed and there's definitely no washers there :smile: Those you will need to heat if you want to remove them.

Your last photo is correct. You want a gap between the motor and the drive wheel adapter. The second photo might have tape in-between instead of a washer.

It's a T20 Star/Torx bit.
```

---

## \#2095 Posted by: Richcan Posted at: 2019-07-26T20:10:40.150Z Reads: 165

```
I think you just want a spacer/washer up against the inner bearing race. So same diameter as it can rotate freely with bearing. It‚Äôs just to space wheel core from rubbing. If you find washer you might need to file down the outside diameter so it can rest up against the rotating equipment. That‚Äôs my guess till we can all see what it looks like under that core adapter? Good Luck!
```

## \#2100 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-07-26T21:46:34.719Z Reads: 174

```
I'll try and make a video tutorial tomorrow.

You can replace the tape for a standard M4 washer and they will fit in-between the bolt holes for the drive wheel adapter.

Depends how severe the issue is. If you can help it, you want nothing restricting the motor movement. You don't want to add any resistance if you don't have too.
```

## \#2128 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-07-30T23:31:32.385Z Reads: 167

```
@Jansen - Good to know! Hope you're enjoying it. :smile:

I'd try and keep it 120C / 248F max. I've always found that climbing steep hills back to back will increase temps esp. if you lose momentum on a hill. Magnets are good up to 150C / 302F.

We'll test more soon with the AT Tires also to see what kind of temps we get.
```

---
## \#2129 Posted by: ThomasL Posted at: 2019-07-31T08:10:05.879Z Reads: 169

```
@Jansen took them on a very long trip (80km) with hills and stuff. Took them to 67km/h (based on Sport tracker, 110mm big wheels, 12s5p on the 90kv). They never reached more than 70 degrees C, and Unity 55 degrees C.

I believe for them to reach high temperature, I would have to be 100kg, and climb massive hill at 50km/h
```

## \#2149 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-08-02T13:20:25.174Z Reads: 168

```
@ThomasL Thanks for the updates.

Are you using the temp sensors on the motors?

Ultimately, you don't want to get them too hot. There's a breaking point. Just as long as you don't go past it you won't burn out a motor and everything will be fine if you let it cool down. Typical for all motors but that threshold is more prone for a direct drive/hub motor.

As far as AT Kit will be soon. Waiting on stock on tires + testing the DD adapter which should be soon. Price should be about $199.99 including adapters.
```

## \#2159 Posted by: Pedrodemio Posted at: 2019-08-02T23:19:31.791Z Reads: 173

```
For people with overheating problems you guys should try Statorade, lots of data of using it on ebike hubs

https://www.ebikes.ca/shop/electric-bicycle-parts/motor-hardware/cooling-mods/statorade.html

The problem is that since the hanger is almost all motor, there is almost no surface area for the heat to be dissipated, and the air gap between the stator and magnets is a awful heat conductor, Statorade bridge that cap and turns the hole motor can in a heat sink

@torqueboards maybe you could do some tests with it and include it as a upgrade for those who want to push the drives
```

## \#2169 Posted by: skatardude10 Posted at: 2019-08-06T04:09:09.375Z Reads: 171

```
I run 80A per motor, pretty sure that is the recommended max amp limit. 4000-4500 watts per motor I think? 

12S is common, that or any other voltage common for eboards should be fine.

That's really all you need to set these up, just battery settings based off your battery specs, motor settings based off that and tweak to your liking. I don't think a vesc setup tutorial needs to be included, there are tons of tutorials, written and video online already.

As for max temp cutoffs, I just stick with vesc tool defaults, 85C I think. It's way lower than what the magnets can handle which is I think around 120-130C. Just be conservative if you want to play it safe with cutoffs. If you do CPU overclocking, I think of 120-130C as the Tj Max... But long term stable temps are usually safe being much lower than that.
```

---

## \#2177 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-08-09T16:44:00.288Z Reads: 164

```
@rideTastic Unless the hanger grew 10-20mm. The motor shrunk 10-20mm. Which aren't really possible.

The motor was designed to slip out of the hanger axle without a wheel attached.

1. It's most likely going to be a loose axle (which you would need to check).
2. The fitment to your wheel (which you would need to check).

You'll need to give me more details to work on instead of shifting the motor back and forth and saying it doesn't work.
```

## \#2183 Posted by: skatardude10 Posted at: 2019-08-10T00:14:16.859Z Reads: 166

```
The motors are designed to slide off the axles, and if a wheel is not installed they should slide off. If they are sliding around with a wheel installed, you might have to adjust your wheels bearing spacers or take the motor off and tighten the axles on tight. To make sure the axles don't come loose, I used isopropyl alcohol to clean whatever loctite they used off the axle threads, and dribbled some loctite blue on, and tightened the crap out of them and didn't ride hard for about 24 hours for the loctite to fully dry.

If your wheels are on, axles tight, bearing spacers installed correctly, axle nut torqued down a bit (correctly sized spacers absolutely necessary for this, with speed rings or not on one side or the other to get wheel as close as possible to drive motor without strain on the motor), and the motor is still sliding around, I'd double check all the screws on the motor are tight. If they are all tight, how much is the motor moving? Just a bit along the hangar, in and out from the wheel? Maybe space your wheel a bit closer to the motor to tighten it up? Curious...
```

---

## \#2217 Posted by: skatardude10 Posted at: 2019-08-29T17:05:12.505Z Reads: 181

```
You're right, the startup cogging in the beginning sounds normal. Regarding the rest of the sound, if those were mine i'd ride them for a bit and see if it gets worse. I wouldn't push them too hard for a little while until you know its either getting worse or better. If your motors are faulty you should have no issues getting them replaced or fixed, and if it goes away that's even better. One of my motors sounded a little odd and didn't spin as well as the other when I first got them but after a couple rides out they both spin perfect and now I couldn't tell you which motor it was.
```

## \#2252 Posted by: Menjos Posted at: 2019-09-16T20:18:54.840Z Reads: 175

```
Finally everything is setup properly. The motors are running smoothly now in FOC and without any issues. Also had a high frequency whining noise after the first day as described by others, a few drops "bones speed cream" on the inner bearings and it's gone. Also had a bit of rattling as the motors are sitting on the trucks with a tiny bit of play, put some insolation tape in there, also gone now. 

![IMG_20190911_192926|690x460](upload://561xSSchO1xBvnrXfsfDMZpyXjA.jpeg)
![IMG_20190911_200548|690x459](upload://416YAHz0qCuNBms8sDZ4bTeVwkH.jpeg)
```

---

Hanger width is also massive, was thinking about cutting out some rubber from so I can mount the offset wheels in reverse. But I'm actually starting to like the wide hangers, adds a lot of stability.

## \#2262 Posted by: Ubbiedude Posted at: 2019-09-18T20:13:31.457Z Reads: 171

```
I just mounted the revised axle stubs on my trucs and now the motor can won't sit against the base of the truck, the new axle stubs are 2mm wider... ![20190918_221132|690x388](upload://dASfMBxr84xKAVSJKgsawdSD1g8.jpeg)
```

---
## \#2263 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2019-09-18T22:42:13.556Z Reads: 169

```
The axle isn‚Äôt the issue because the motor will fit over the axle and the hanger. Most likely you might have a tighter tolerance. You can use a soft mallet to push the motor in more and or try that motor on the opposite side.

I‚Äôd also take the wheel off and mount without the wheel first. Try that first. :slight_smile:
```

## \#2275 Posted by: Menjos Posted at: 2019-10-24T15:15:40.803Z Reads: 141

```
There is actually quite a difference, the real diameter of the storm esk8's is only about 102mm, not 105 - and that's only for the center of the wheel. So I guess they would have about 20-25% less volume. Also visually they are ok for my built, while the Torqueboards just looks too massive. That being said, I might change my mind. I still have to give them a try! So far the rubber wheels are perfect for my daily commute, with lot's of steep terrain. I love the rubber. I don't think they will hurt range that much in this scenario, and I don't mind either.
```

---
## \#2276 Posted by: Deathjunior Posted at: 2019-10-24T20:06:32.914Z Reads: 147

```
Well I out a couple hundred miles on the storm esk8 and between my gear drive and the rubber wheels I averaged 15 miles on a 12s4p Samsung 30q battery back. I should mention I got 20-22 miles on my 97mm urethanes with the same belt drive.  As for my 110mm wheels and direct drive I'm hitting 25 miles fairly consistantly. The rubber wheels were softer and more comfortable but they have a ton more rolling resistance. 

 ![IMG_20181205_202106_547|500x500](upload://uW4hvFPlXY2q6avngxHyN8egQ4O.jpeg) 
 
![20190915_182428|531x500](upload://aDJXYqnQriDmUvbix2FNyvGltn6.jpeg) 

![IMG_20180714_205948_252|500x500](upload://giENXdugXrl2tHbXC6HijzQNwCg.jpeg) 

My boards had a lot of iterations. And as of now I have a belt drive back on it and I'll be testing out the tires I helped developed for torqueboards. So excited. 
![20191022_142455|375x500](upload://zSuIDC4TDWY7zfhxlFnD0EWvFX9.jpeg)
```

## \#2286 Posted by: Menjos Posted at: 2019-11-05T17:10:35.953Z Reads: 131

```
It's a generic deck that you can find on places like alibaba, taobao, diyeboard.com. They are stable and comfortable for riders up to about 85kg. ```
```

## \#2289 Posted by: Menjos Posted at: 2019-11-13T20:21:57.203Z Reads: 120

```
Had similar issues, but it was just a matter of applying bearing oil regularly. The bearings are quite exposed and collect a lot of dirt, so I also try to keep them clean.
```

## \#2314 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2019-12-07T18:12:06.322Z Reads: 99

```
[quote="ElectricCoast, post:2313, topic:61152"]
ased my battery current max regen to -30 and it‚Äôs still the same. I‚Äôm completely befuddled. My Kaly with gear drives are s
[/quote]

[quote="ElectricCoast, post:2313, topic:61152"]
@Eboosted osted 've increased my battery current max regen to -30 and it‚Äôs still the same.
[/quote]

That's impossible, there must be a noticeable braking force going from -15A to -30A.

You will have a stronger braking force but only at high speeds over 25km/hr, at lower speeds there will no much change, so the next question would be, are you braking in low speeds or high speeds?
```

## \#2328 Posted by: love2scoot Posted at: 2019-12-17T17:18:12.776Z Reads: 89

```
I want to understand this a bit better.  Since direct drive does not have the torque advantage at lower speeds that belts offer (since there is no gear reduction), the braking curve is different.  While brakes will work just fine at higher speeds, once speeds get below a certain threshold the motor isn't spinning fast enough to provide sufficient stopping power with regenerative breaking. Using the Smart Current Reverse would essentially apply current in reverse which would add to the stopping power of the board below this threshold.  Adding AT wheels to the mix would then compound this state and raise the speed threshold at which the Smart Current Reverse would need to be applied.  I would imagine the challenge here would be in making the braking curve feel continuous as it transitions from regenerative to current reverse.  Does this correctly describe the DD + Smart Current Reverse approach?
```

---

## \#2337 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2020-01-02T05:36:48.433Z Reads: 75

```
If your bms is wired for charge/discharge then that might be your issue, you will need to use a new bms with more rated current or change the wiring of the BMS to be used only for discharge
```

## \#2344 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2020-01-02T18:23:58.202Z Reads: 69

```
You should ask the battery builder how was the BMS wired?, charge/discharge or charge only.

Please also ask what BMS, brand and model and maximum current specs, he did install. Some BMS cutout while on maximum current and you loose everything from brakes to power.
```
